CITY OF SAN MATEO
DRAFT ORDINANCE
An Ordinance amending San Mateo Municipal Code Chapter 23.24 “Energy Code,” of Title 23, “Building and 
Construction,” to amend the California Energy Code, 2022 Edition and amending San Mateo Municipal Code 
Chapter 23.70 “Green Building Code,” of Title 23, “Building and Construction,” to amend the California Green 
Building Standards Code, 2022 Edition
WHEREAS, the City of San Mateo’s (City) Climate Action Plan recommends the City review local 
amendments to the California Energy Code and the Green Building Standards Code to promote building 
electrification, energy efficiency, and electric vehicle infrastructure; and
WHEREAS, California Energy Code and Green Building Standards Code, 2022 Edition, were adopted by 
the City of San Mateo on November 7, 2022 with local amendments to require all-electric new construction and 
electric-readiness and electric appliances during residential building remodels; and
WHEREAS, due to a federal court decision, in early 2024, the City suspended enforcement of local 
amendments that prohibited the installation of gas infrastructure; and
WHEREAS, this presented an opportunity to replace the City’s reach code to encourage sustainable new 
construction; and
WHEREAS, the proposed Ordinance amends the California Energy Code to require energy compliance 
margins for newly constructed buildings and require electric-readiness when gas infrastructure is installed; and
WHEREAS, the proposed Ordinance appeals local amendments to the California Green Building Code 
that are unenforceable due to the federal court decision; and
WHEREAS, the proposed Ordinance amends the California Green Building Code to make a minor edit to 
the electric-readiness requirements to promote consistency with the 2022 Energy Code electric-readiness 
requirements for new construction; and
WHEREAS, California Health and Safety Code Sections 17922, 17958, 17958.5, 17958.7, and 18941.5 
authorizes the City to make local amendments to the California Energy Code and Green Building Standards Code 
upon express findings that the local amendments are reasonably necessary due to local climatic, geographical, 
or topographical conditions; and
WHEREAS, concurrent with this Ordinance, the City Council of the City of San Mateo has adopted a 
resolution adopting express findings in support of local amendments to the California Energy Code and Green 
Building Standards Code, 2022 Edition; and
WHEREAS, Public Resources Code Section 25402.1(h)2 and Section 10-106 of the Building Energy 
Efficiency Standards (Standards) establish a process which allows local adoption of energy standards that are 
more stringent than the statewide Standards, provided that such local standards are cost effective, and the 
California Energy Commission finds that the standards will require building to be designed to consume no more 
energy than permitted by the California Energy Code; and 
65 of 426

--- page 66 ---
WHEREAS, staff has reviewed the cost effectiveness studies prepared by the California Statewide Codes 
and Standards Reach Code Program and associated study data and find them sufficient to illustrate compliance 
with the requirements set forth under California Administrative Code Chapter 10-106; and
WHEREAS, that such modifications will result in designs that consume less energy than they would 
under the 2022 State Energy Code through the California Statewide Codes and Standards Reach Code Program, 
has performed cost effectiveness analyses as required by the California Energy Commission for the local 
amendments to the California Energy Code contained in this Ordinance which is hereby incorporated by 
reference; and
WHEREAS, based upon these analyses, the San Mateo City Council finds that the local amendments to 
the California Energy Code contained in the Ordinance have at least one cost effective pathway and will require 
buildings to be designed to consume no more energy than permitted by the California Energy Code.
NOW, THEREFORE, THE COUNCIL OF THE CITY OF SAN MATEO ORDAINS AS FOLLOWS:
Section 1. Section 23.24.020 of the San Mateo Municipal Code is amended as follows:
23.24.020 Local Amendment to Definitions
(a) Energy Code subsection 100.1(b) is amended to include the following definitions:
Electric Heating Appliance. A device that produces heat energy to create a warm environment by the 
application of electric power to resistance elements, refrigerant compressors, or dissimilar material 
junctions, as defined in the California Mechanical Code.
Kitchen, institutional commercial. A kitchen dedicated to a foodservice establishment that provides 
meals at institutions including schools, colleges and universities, hospitals, correctional facilities, private 
cafeterias, nursing homes, and other buildings or structures in which care or supervision is provided to 
occupants.
Kitchen, quick-service commercial. A kitchen dedicated to an establishment primarily engaged in 
providing fast food, fast casual, or limited services. Food and drink may be consumed on premises, taken 
out, or delivered to the customer’s location.
Net Free Area (NFA). The total unobstructed area of the air gaps between louver and grille slats in a 
vent through which air can pass. The narrowest distance between two slats, perpendicular to the 
surface of both slats is the air gap height. The narrowest width of the gap is the air gap width. The NFA is 
the air gap height multiplied by the air gap width multiplied by the total number of air gaps between 
slats in the vent.
Section 2. Section 23.24.030 of the San Mateo Municipal Code is amended as follows:

23.24.030 Electric-readiness and Energy Performance of Nonresidential Buildings
(a) Energy Code Section 120.2 “Required Controls for Space-Conditioning Systems” is amended to add a 
new subsection (l) to read as follows:
(l) HVAC Hot Water Temperature. Zones that use hot water for space heating shall be designed 
for a hot water supply temperature of no greater than 130°F.
(b) Energy Code Section 120.6 “Mandatory Requirements for Covered Processes” is amended to add a 
new subsection (k) to read as follows:
(k) Mandatory requirements for commercial kitchens. Electric Readiness for Newly Constructed 
Commercial Kitchens shall meet the following requirements:
1. Quick-service commercial kitchens and institutional commercial kitchens shall include 
a dedicated branch circuit wiring and outlet that would be accessible to cookline 
appliances and shall meet all of the following requirements: 
A. The branch circuit conductors shall be rated at 50 amps minimum.
B. The electrical service panel shall have a minimum capacity of 800 connected 
amps.
2. The electrical service panel shall be sized to accommodate an additional either 208v 
or 240v 50-amp breaker.
Exception 1 to Section 120.6(k): healthcare facilities. 
Exception 2 to Section 120.6(k): all-electric commercial kitchens.
(c) Energy Code subsection 130.0(a) is amended to read as follows:
The design and installation of all lighting systems and equipment in nonresidential and hotel/motel 
buildings, outdoor lighting, and electrical power distribution systems within the scope of Section 
100.0(a), shall comply with the applicable provisions of Sections 130.0 through 130.6. 
NOTE: The requirements of Sections 130.0 through 130.6 apply to newly constructed buildings. Section 
141.0 specifies which requirements of Sections 130.0 through 130.6 also apply to additions and 
alterations to existing buildings.
(d) Energy Code Subchapter 4 “Nonresidential and Hotel/Motel Occupancies – Mandatory Requirements 
for Lighting Systems and Equipment, and Electrical Power Distribution Systems” is amended to add a new 
section 130.6 “Electric Readiness Requirements for Systems Using Gas or Propane” and read as follows:
130.6 Electric Readiness Requirements for Systems Using Gas or Propane  
67 of 426

--- page 68 ---
Where nonresidential systems using gas or propane are installed, the construction drawings shall 
indicate electrical infrastructure and physical space accommodating the future installation of an electric 
heating appliance in the following ways, as certified by a registered design professional or licensed 
electrical contractor.
(a) Branch circuit wiring, electrically isolated and designed to serve all electric heating appliances 
in accordance with manufacturer requirements and the California Electrical Code, including the 
appropriate voltage, phase, minimum amperage, and an electrical receptacle or junction box 
within five feet of the appliance that is accessible with no obstructions. Appropriately sized 
conduit may be installed in lieu of conductors; and 
(b) Labeling of both ends of the unused conductors or conduit shall be with “For Future 
Electrical Appliance”; and
(c) Reserved circuit breakers in the electrical panel for each branch circuit, appropriately labeled 
(e.g. “Reserved for Future Electric Range”), and positioned on the opposite end of the panel 
supply conductor connection; and
(d) Connected subpanels, panelboards, switchboards, busbars, and transformers shall be sized 
to serve the future electric heating appliances. The electrical capacity requirements shall be 
adjusted for demand factors in accordance with the California Electric Code; and 
(e) Physical space for future electric heating appliances, including equipment footprint, and if 
needed a pathway reserved for routing of ductwork to heat pump evaporator(s), shall be 
depicted on the construction drawings. The footprint necessary for future electric heating 
appliances may overlap with non-structural partitions and with the location of currently 
designed combustion equipment.
(e) Energy Code Section 140.0 “Performance and Prescriptive Compliance Approaches” is amended to 
read as follows:
Nonresidential and hotel/motel buildings shall comply with all of the following:
(a) The requirements of Sections 100.0 through 110.12 applicable to the building project 
(mandatory measures for all buildings).
(b) The requirements of Sections 120.0 through 130.6 (mandatory measures for nonresidential 
and high-rise residential and hotel/motel buildings).
(c) Either the performance compliance approach (energy budgets) specified in Section 140.1, or 
the prescriptive compliance approach specified in Section 140.2 for the Climate Zone in which 
the building will be located.  Climate zones are shown in FIGURE 100.1-A.
NOTE to Section 140.0(c): The Commission periodically updates, publishes and makes available 
to interested persons and local enforcement agencies precise descriptions of the Climate Zones,

which is available by zip code boundaries depicted in the Reference Joint Appendices along with

NOTE to Section 140.0: The requirements of Sections 140.1 through 140.10 apply to newly constructed 
buildings.  Section 141.0 specifies which requirements of Section 140.1 through 140.10 also apply to 
additions or alterations to existing buildings.
(f) Energy Code Section 140.1 “Performance Approach: Energy Budgets” is amended to read as follows:
A building complies with the performance approach provided that:
1. The time-dependent valuation (TDV) energy budget calculated for the Proposed Design 
Building under Subsection (b) is no greater than the TDV energy budget calculated for the 
Standard Design Building under Subsection (a), and
2. The source energy budget calculated for the proposed design building under Subsection (b) 
has a source energy compliance margin, relative to the energy budget calculated for the 
standard design building under Subsection (a), of at least 7 percent for all nonresidential 
occupancies.
Exception 1 to 140.1 item 2. A source energy compliance margin of 0 percent or greater 
is required when nonresidential occupancies are designed with single zone space-
conditioning systems complying with Section 140.4(a)2.
Exception 2 to 140.1 item 2. Where it is technically infeasible to implement the 
performance approach standards, exceptions are subject to review and approval at the 
discretion of the Community Development Director, or his/her designee.
(g) Energy Code subsections 140.1(a)-(c) are adopted without modification.

(b) Performance Standards. A building complies with the performance standards if the energy 
consumption calculated for the proposed design building is no greater than the energy budget 
calculated for the standard design building using Commission-certified compliance software as 
specified by the Alternative Calculation Methods Approval Manual, as specified in sub-sections 
1, 2 and 3 below.
1. Newly Constructed Buildings. The Energy Budget for newly constructed buildings is 
expressed in terms of the Energy Design Ratings, which are based on source energy and 
time-dependent valuation (TDV) energy. The Energy Design Rating 1 (EDR1) is based on 
source energy. The Energy Design Rating 2 (EDR2) is based on TDV energy and has two 
components, the Energy Efficiency Design Rating, and the Solar Electric Generation and 
Demand Flexibility Design Rating. The total Energy Design Rating shall account for both 
the Energy Efficiency Design Rating and the Solar Electric Generation and Demand 
Flexibility Design Rating. The proposed building shall separately comply with the Source 
Energy Design Rating, Energy Efficiency Design Rating and the Total Energy Design 
Rating.  A building complies with the performance approach if the TDV energy budget 
calculated for the proposed design building is no greater than the TDV energy budget 
calculated for the Standard Design Building AND Source Energy compliance margin of at 
least 9, relative to the Source Energy Design Rating 1 calculated for the Standard Design 
building.
Exception 1 to Section 150.1(b)1. A community shared solar electric generation 
system, or other renewable electric generation system, and/or community 
shared battery storage system, which provides dedicated power, utility energy 
reduction credits, or payments for energy bill reductions, to the permitted 
building and is approved by the Energy Commission as specified in Title 24, Part 
1, Section 10-115, may offset part or all of the solar electric generation system 
Energy Design Rating required to comply with the Standards, as calculated 
according to methods established by the Commission in the Residential ACM 
Reference Manual.
Exception 2 to Section 150.1(b)1. A newly constructed building with a 
conditioned floor area less than 1,500 square feet shall achieve a Source Energy 
compliance margin of 4 or greater, relative to the Source Energy Design Rating 1 
calculated for the Standard Design building.
70 of 426

--- page 71 ---
Exception 3 to Section 150.1(b)1. A newly constructed building with a 
conditioned floor area less than 625 square feet shall achieve a Source Energy 
compliance margin of 0 or greater, relative to the Source Energy Design Rating 1 
calculated for the Standard Design building.
Exception 4 to Section 150.1(b)1. A newly constructed Accessory Dwelling Unit, 
as defined by San Mateo Municipal Code Section 27.04.165(a), shall achieve a 
Source Energy compliance margin of 0 or greater, relative to the Source Energy 
Design Rating 1 calculated for the Standard Design building.
(c) Energy Code subsections 150.1(b)2, 150.1(b)3, and 150.1(c) are adopted without amendments.

(d) Individual Heat Pump Water Heater Ready. Systems using gas or propane water

pump shall be 2.0 square feet per input 10,000 BTU per hour of the gas

or propane water heating system, and the minimum linear dimension of

per input 10,000 BTU per hour of the gas or propane water heating

MEETING DATE:
January 21, 2025 
SUBJECT:
Parks and Recreation — Classification Updates 
RECOMMENDATION:
Adopt a Resolution to approve the revised job specifications for the Landscape Laborer and Landscape Maintenance 
Worker I/II to reflect a flexible staffed series pursuant to the recent MOU agreement. 
BACKGROUND:
On October 7, 2024, the City Council approved a new memorandum of understanding (MOU) with SEIU which included 
language updating the Landscape Laborer classification to become part of the Landscape Maintenance Worker I/II 
classification series. This change allows for more efficient staffing and growth opportunities. Approving this change to the 
job specifications will allow the implementation of the approved updates. 
BUDGET IMPACT:
The consolidation of the Landscape Laborer with the Landscape Maintenance Worker I/II positions into one flexibly classed 
position was included in the 2024-25 adopted budget so this will have no fiscal impact. 
ENVIRONMENTAL DETERMINATION:
This classification update is not a project subject to CEQA, because it is a government fiscal activity which does not involve 
any commitment to any specific project which may result in a potentially significant physical impact on the environment. 
(CEQA Guidelines Section 15378(b)(4).)
NOTICE PROVIDED
All meeting noticing requirements were met.
ATTACHMENTS
Att 1 —Proposed Resolution
              Exhibit A —Job Specification Landscape Laborer and Landscape Maintenance Worker I/II
Att 2 — Job Specification with Tracked Changes

Lourdes Coles, Senior Human Resources Analyst
lcoles@cityofsanmateo.org

CITY OF SAN MATEO
RESOLUTION NO. __ (2025)
APPROVING THE CLASSIFICATION UPDATES IN THE PARKS AND RECREATION DEPARTMENT
WHEREAS, pursuant to the San Mateo Municipal Code Section 2.57.030(d), approval of new 
classifications and related job specifications, salary schedules, compensation changes, elimination or 
reinstatement of positions, reallocation of positions, reclassifications, and revisions of job specifications 
must be approved by City Council Resolution; and
WHEREAS, the proposed changes as detailed below reflect the new Memorandum of 
Understanding (MOU) with SEIU which included language updating the Landscape Laborer classification 
to become part of the Landscape Maintenance Worker I/II classification series. This change allows for 
more efficient staffing and growth opportunities; and
WHEREAS, the proposed job specifications for the classifications of Landscape Laborer and 
Landscape Maintenance Worker I/II are attached hereto as Exhibit A and incorporated by reference; and
WHEREAS, the employee associations representing the impacted classifications have been 
informed of the classification updates and have not brought forth any objections or concerns.
NOW, THEREFORE, THE CITY COUNCIL OF THE CITY OF SAN MATEO, CALIFORNIA, HEREBY 
RESOLVES that: 
1.
The classification updates are not subject to California Environmental Quality Act (CEQA 
Guidelines Section 15061(b)(3)) because it can be seen with certainty that they will not 
cause a physical change in the environment; and
2.
The job specification for the classifications of Landscape Laborer and Landscape 
Maintenance Worker I/II attached hereto as Exhibit A are approved.

Exhibit A
LANDSCAPE LABORER
LANDSCAPE MAINTENANCE WORKER I/II
DEFINITION
Under supervision, performs a variety of skilled gardening and landscape maintenance duties 
associated with the development, repair, and maintenance of public landscaped areas.  Operates a 
wide variety of park and/or golf course equipment; may operate various mowing equipment to 
cut a variety of turfgrass areas throughout the City; and to perform related work as required.
Landscape Laborers and Landscape Maintenance Workers I/II are found in the Parks and Golf 
Course Divisions of the Parks and Recreation Department.  Incumbents in these classifications 
may work individually on occasion, but primarily in combination with other Landscape 
Maintenance Workers and Landscape Laborers as a crew assigned to specific gardening and 
maintenance projects in City parks, municipal golf course, athletic fields, or other City facilities. 
DISTINGUISHING CHARACTERISTICS
Landscape Laborer - This is the entry level class in the Landscape Maintenance Worker class 
series.  This position must be adaptive and work well with others.  The laborer will be the 
primary position for all manual tasks.  The individual must have good work habits and display 
good judgment and be able to work safely.  The position must demonstrate the ability to operate 
a full range of hand tools and light engine equipment or acquire the skills after training.
Landscape Maintenance Worker I - This is the mid-level class in the Landscape Maintenance 
Worker class series.  The positions in this class will normally perform most of the duties required 
of the Landscape Maintenance Worker I and II. However, as compared to the Landscape 
Maintenance Worker II, they are not expected to function at the same skill level and will 
normally exercise less discretion and judgment on matters related to work procedures and 
methods.  Work is usually supervised while in progress and fits a pattern which has been 
established and explained before the work is started.  Generally, changes in procedures or 
exceptions are explained in detail as they arise. Work assignments vary depending upon the 
function to which individuals are assigned and periodic work assignment transfers occur both for 
training purposes and to meet departmental staffing and work productivity requirements.
Landscape Maintenance Worker II - This is the journey level class in the Landscape 
Maintenance Worker series.  Positions in this class are flexibly staffed and are normally filled by 
advancement from the Landscape Maintenance Worker I class, or when filled from the outside, 
require prior experience in the maintenance of landscaped areas.  Appointment to the higher 
class requires that the employee be performing substantially the full range of duties for the class 
and meet the qualification standards for the class.  All positions assigned to the class require the 
80 of 426

--- page 81 ---
ability to work independently, exercising judgment and initiative.  For positions assigned to the 
golf course and landscape mowing crews, the demonstrated ability to operate the full range of 
park equipment normally utilized by the City in a safe, efficient and proper manner is a 
prerequisite for being assigned to the class.  Work assignments vary depending upon the function 
to which individuals are assigned and periodic work assignment transfers occur both for training 
purposes and to meet departmental staffing and work productivity requirements.
SUPERVISION RECEIVED AND EXERCISED
Receives general supervision from the Senior Park Landscape Maintenance Worker or Golf 
Course Maintenance Supervisor.  Technical or functional supervision may also be provided by 
higher-level department personnel.  May provide supervision for seasonal (per diem) workers.
EXAMPLES OF DUTIES - Depending upon assignment, duties may include, but are not 
limited to, the following:
Landscape Maintenance/Horticulture
Maintains grounds and plantings in City parks, recreation facilities, playground areas, municipal 
building grounds, and street median islands 
Maintains designated landscape effects through mowing, edging, pruning, weeding, fertilizing, 
cultivating, planting lawns, shrubs, ground cover, trees, and flowerbeds. 
Picks up, cleans and removes debris and trash from walkways, picnic areas, play areas, 
restrooms, parking lots, drainage ditches and culverts. 
Performs minor routine maintenance and repair on sprinklers and irrigation equipment. 
Operates various power mowers, edgers, line trimmers, backpack blowers, sprayers, chain saws, 
aerators and other power equipment.
Assists in the mixing and applications of various pesticides, including herbicides.
Drive vehicles used to transport materials, tools, and equipment as required.
Assists in installation, minor repair and maintenance of parks and recreation playground 
equipment or furniture.
Work cooperatively and effectively with co-workers.
Respond to inquiries from the public.
Fully utilize the computerized work systems in accordance with workflow processes.
Work alone or as a member of a crew.
81 of 426

--- page 82 ---
Landscape Maintenance/Equipment Operation
Maintain and prepare athletic fields including dragging and watering baseball diamonds.
Operate complex mowing equipment; operate trucks, tractors, front end loaders, spray rigs, 
trenchers, and utilize a variety of hand and power tools in park maintenance work.
Fully utilize the computerized work systems in accordance with workflow processes.
Work alone or as a member of a crew.
Drive vehicles used to transport materials, tools and equipment as required.
Aerify, fertilize, seed and top-dress athletic fields, and other associated turfgrass areas.
Assist in the mixing and application of various pesticides, including herbicides
Work cooperatively and effectively with co-workers.
Perform routine preventative maintenance on mowing equipment and hand and power tools used 
in the course of work.
Performs minor routine maintenance and repair on sprinklers and irrigation equipment.
Landscape Maintenance/Golf Course
Perform routine preventive maintenance on mowing and hand and power tools used in the course 
of work.
Install, clean and rake sand traps.
Mow and trim tees and greens.
Assist in the construction, renovation, and maintenance of fairways, tees, sand traps, greens and 
other landscaped areas.
Apply pesticides and fertilizers to turf areas.
Aerify, fertilize, seed and top-dress greens complexes, and other associated turfgrass areas.
Perform routine maintenance on sprinklers and irrigation equipment.
Assist with irrigation repairs on main lines, lateral lines, valves, and heads under supervision 
from the Irrigation Specialist.
82 of 426

--- page 83 ---
Assist with small equipment maintenance or repairs under supervision. 
Fully utilize the computerized work systems in accordance with workflow processes.
Water, weed, trim, renovate, fertilize and perform mowing of golf course.
Respond to inquiries from the public.
Drive vehicles to transport materials, tools, and equipment as required.
Work alone or as a member of a crew.
Work cooperatively and effectively with co-workers.
If assigned to the golf course, golf course setup procedures including but not limited to: cup 
cutting, proper pin location movement, dew removal and tee marker placement. 
If assigned to the golf course, perform routine maintenance on greens, fairways and tees. 
Early mornings and rotational weekend and holiday scheduling are required.
QUALIFICATIONS

Basic methods, tools, materials, and equipment used in grounds maintenance work.

maintenance work, as assigned.
Use computers and handheld electronic devices in the course of work.
Work cooperatively and effectively with co-workers and provide general assistance to the 
public.
Ability to work weekends and holidays as required.

Maintenance Worker I with the City of San Mateo.
LICENSE AND CERTIFICATE

record. 
ADA Special Requirement:

Ability to sit, stand, walk, kneel, crouch, squat, stoop, reach, twist, and lift 80 pounds; exposure 
to cold, heat, outdoors, chemicals, dust and mechanical hazards.

LANDSCAPE LABORER
LANDSCAPE MAINTENANCE WORKER I/II
DEFINITION
Under supervision, performs a variety of skilled gardening and landscape maintenance duties 
associated with the development, repair, and maintenance of public landscaped areas.  Operates a wide 
variety of park and/or golf course equipment; may operate various mowing equipment to cut a variety 
of turfgrass areas throughout the City; and to perform related work as required.
Landscape Laborers and Landscape Maintenance Workers I/II are found in the Parks and Golf Course 
Divisions of the Parks and Recreation Department.  Incumbents in these classifications may work 
individually on occasion, but primarily in combination with other Landscape Maintenance Workers 
and Landscape Laborers as a crew assigned to specific gardening and maintenance projects in City 
parks, municipal golf course, athletic fields, or other City facilities. 
DISTINGUISHING CHARACTERISTICS
Landscape Laborer - This is the entry level class in the Landscape Maintenance Worker class series.  
This position must be adaptive and work well with others.  The laborer will be the primary position for 
all manual tasks.  The individual must have good work habits and display good judgment and be able 
to work safely.  The position must demonstrate the ability to operate a full range of hand tools and light 
engine equipment or acquire the skills after training.
Landscape Maintenance Worker I - This is the mid-level class in the Landscape Maintenance 
Worker class series.  The positions in this class will normally perform most of the duties required of 
the Landscape Maintenance Worker I and II. However, as compared to the Landscape Maintenance 
Worker II, they are not expected to function at the same skill level and will normally exercise less 
discretion and judgment on matters related to work procedures and methods.  Work is usually 
supervised while in progress and fits a pattern which has been established and explained before the 
work is started.  Generally, changes in procedures or exceptions are explained in detail as they arise. 
Work assignments vary depending upon the function to which individuals are assigned and periodic 
work assignment transfers occur both for training purposes and to meet departmental staffing and work 
productivity requirements.
Landscape Maintenance Worker II - This is the journey level class in the Landscape Maintenance 
Worker series.  Positions in this class are flexibly staffed and are normally filled by advancement from 
the Landscape Maintenance Worker I class, or when filled from the outside, require prior experience in 
the maintenance of landscaped areas.  Appointment to the higher class requires that the employee be 
performing substantially the full range of duties for the class and meet the qualification standards for 
87 of 426

--- page 88 ---
the class.  All positions assigned to the class require the ability to work independently, exercising 
judgment and initiative.  For positions assigned to the golf course and landscape mowing crews, the 
demonstrated ability to operate the full range of park equipment normally utilized by the City in a safe, 
efficient and proper manner is a prerequisite for being assigned to the class.  Work assignments vary 
depending upon the function to which individuals are assigned and periodic work assignment transfers 
occur both for training purposes and to meet departmental staffing and work productivity requirements.
SUPERVISION RECEIVED AND EXERCISED
Receives general supervision from the Senior Park Landscape Maintenance Worker or Golf Course 
Maintenance Supervisor.  Technical or functional supervision may also be provided by higher-level 
department personnel.  May provide supervision for seasonal (per diem) workers.

Work alone or as a member of a crew.

Agenda Number: {{item.number}} Section Name: {{section.name}: Account Number: 25-3112 File ID: {{item.tracking_number}}
TO: City Council
FROM: Alex Khojikian, City Manager

MEETING DATE: January 21, 2025
SUBJECT:

Historic Policy Update Effort Professional Services — Appropriation and Agreement

RECOMMENDATION:

Review and provide direction on historic preservation policies, including: the adoption of a Resolution to appropriate
$328,743 (Option 1) or $394,450 (Option 2) from the Advance Planning Fund to the Historic Policy Update project, with
each option corresponding to a different project schedule; and approve an agreement with Rincon Consultants for
community outreach and technical support related to historic policy and code amendments; and authorize the City
Manager to execute the agreement in substantially the form presented and to revise it as needed based on the selected
option.

BACKGROUND:

The Proposed Resolution to appropriate funds from the Advance Planning Fund to the Historic Policy Update project, if
Option 1 or Option 2 are selected, it is included as Attachment 1, and the professional services agreement with Rincon
Consultants to provide community outreach, historic policy and code amendment technical support is included as
Attachment 2.

General Plan 2040

San Mateo’s General Plan 2040, which was adopted by the City Council on March 18, 2024, sets the policy framework for
how issues such as historic resources and preservation should be addressed. The Community Design and Historic
Resources Element addresses the topic of historic and cultural resources, and includes goals, policies, and actions that
outline the framework for how the City should approach historic resources and preservation. Specifically, Goal CD-5
speaks to preserving the historic and culturally important resources to maintain San Mateo’s special identity and
continuity with the past and includes seven policies and six actions to support achievement of this goal (Attachment 3).

During the adoption process for General Plan 2040, the topic of historic resource preservation generated significant
community interest and comments; with the historic related policies and actions based around this community input and
the final versions based on Council direction. In addition, in the fall 2023, a historic district designation application for the
Baywood Neighborhood was submitted to the State Office of Historic Preservation by the San Mateo Heritage Alliance.
This application resulted in significant community discussions surrounding establishing historic districts, how the
designations are approved at the State and local levels, and questions about the potential impacts of an application and a
subsequent designation on properties within the district. To address questions about the State and local historic review
processes and how historic districts are established, Planning Division staff, with support from historic consultant
Architectural Resources Group (ARG), conducted a community informational meeting (link:
https://www.youtube.com/watch?v=mICAKmxT3w8&t=6s) in February 2024. The City’s Historic Resources webpage (link
here -https://www.cityofsanmateo.org/4775/Historic-Resources) was also updated to provide FAQs related to the historic
district designation process, the City’s permitting process for potential historic resources, and information on how the

Chapter 5

Community Design and Historic Resources Element

GOALS, POLICIES, AND ACTIONS

GOAL CD-5

Preserve historic and culturally important resources to maintain San Mateo’s

special identity and continuity with the past.

POLICIES

Policy CD 5.1

Policy CD 5.2

Policy CD 5.3

oS Policy CD 5.4

Policy CD 5.5

Policy CD 5.6

Comprehensive Approach to Historic Preservation. Implement a comprehensive
approach to historic preservation based on community input and best practices from
State and federal agencies, to find an appropriate balance between preservation with
other important priorities, such as affordable housing production and supporting local
businesses.

Historic Preservation. Actively identify and preserve historic resources and concentrations
of historic resources which convey the flavor of local historical periods, are culturally
significant, or provide an atmosphere of exceptional architectural interest or integrity,
as feasible, when they meet national, State, or local criteria. Historic resources include
individual properties, districts, and sites that maintain San Mateo’s sense of place and
special identity, and enrich our unde’standing of the city’s history and continuity with the
past.

Historic Resources Definition. Define historic resources as buildings, structures, sites, and
districts that are listed in or determined to be eligible for listing in the National Register
of Historic Places and/or California Register of Historical Resources, designated resources
in the 1989 Historic Building Survey Report, and resources found to be eligible through
documentation in a historic resources report.

Public Awareness. Foster public awareness and appreciation of the City’s historic resources
and educate the community about how to preserve and improve these resources. Increase
public appreciation by supporting groups and organizations that provide neighborhood
workshops, public presentations, interpretive signage, and walking tours.

Historic Resources Renovation and Rehabilitation. Promote the renovation and
rehabilitation of historic resources thet conforms to the Secretary of the Interior’s Standards
for Rehabilitation and Guidelines for Rehabilitating Historic Structures and the California
Historical Building Code and prioritize historic structures for available rehabilitation funds.

Historic Preservation Funding. Pursue and promote historic preservation funding sources
to incentivize the protection of historic resources, such as the California Mills Act Property
Tax Abatement Program, Federal and State Historic Preservation Tax Incentives Program,
and State Historic Rehabilitation Tax Credit Program.

General Plan 2040


--- page 119 ---
Chapter 5

Policy CD 5.7

ACTIONS

Community Design and Historic Resources Element

Demolition Alternatives. Require anapplicant to submit alternatives to preserve a historic
resource as part of any planning application that proposes full demolition. Implement
preservation methods unless health and safety requirements cannot be met or the City
Council makes a finding explaining the specific reasons why the social, economic, legal,
technical, or other beneficial aspects of the proposed demolition outweigh the unavoidable
adverse impacts to the historic resource. If a designated historic resource cannot be
preserved, require City approval before the demolition of a historic resource.

Action CD 5.8

Action CD 5.9

Action CD 5.10

Action CD 5.11

Action CD 5.12

Action CD 5.13

Historic Preservation Ordinance. Update the City’s Historic Preservation Ordinance to
create a framework for the designation of historic resources and districts, establish review
and permitting procedures for historic alterations, demolitions or relocations, be consistent
with federal and State standards andguidelines, and align with the other goals and policies
outlined in this Element.

Historic Resources Context Statements. Prepare a citywide historic context statement
to guide future historic resource survey efforts to identify individually eligible resources
and historic districts. If a neighborhcod is identified as a historic district, prepare a more
detailed historic context statement for that individual neighborhood.

Historic Resources Survey. Establish and maintain an inventory of architecturally, culturally,
and historically significant buildings, structures, sites, and districts. Proactively maintain
an up-to-date historic resources inventory by seeking funding opportunities to update
the historic survey. Prepare neighborhood-specific historic context statements prior to
updating the historic resources survey.

Preservation Incentives. Explore the option to create incentives to preserve historic and
cultural resources, such as reducing parking and other prescriptive requirements, allowing
adaptive reuse, or establishing a transfer of development rights program.

Historic Resources Design Standards. Create objective design standards for alterations to
historic resources and contributors to a designated historic district, and new development
adjacent to historic resources within historic districts. Use the Secretary of the Interior’s
Standards as the basis for these objective design standards to ensure projects have a
contextual relationship with land usesand patterns; spatial organization; visual relationships;
cultural and historic values; and the height, massing, design, and materials of historic
resources.

Certified Local Government. Explore the feasibility of becoming a Certified Local
Government (CLG) to become eligible for federal grant funds and technical assistance in
support of historic resource preservetion efforts.

General Plan 2040

HERITAGE ALLIANCE

January 16, 2025

City Council

City of San Mateo
330 W. 20% Avenue
San Mateo, CA 94403

SUBJECT: Support for Context Study and Historic Preservation Ordinance Update

Dear Mayor Newsom and City Council Members:

The San Mateo Heritage Alliance strongly urges the approval of the proposed scope of work to prepare
a context study and to update our historic preservation ordinance. The current ordinance, dating back
to 1993, and the outdated 1989 Historic Building Survey are no longer sufficient to meet the demands of
our growing city while preserving its rich historical legacy.

The Importance of a Context Study

Economic and Efficient: A context study is far more cost-effective than a detailed survey of
each historic property, providing a broad understanding of our city's historical assets at a
fraction of the cost.

Framework for Preservation: It will lay down the groundwork necessary for a citywide historic
resources understanding, informing not just preservation but also future development.

Policy Informed by Study: The study will directly influence the updating of our preservation
policies and ordinance, ensuring they reflect the current state and significance of our historical
resources.

Strategic Planning: By understanding the type, quantity, and location of our historic resources,
we can make informed decisions that balance growth with preservation.

The Necessity to Update the Historic Preservation Ordinance

Cultural and Economic Benefits: As noted in our current ordinance, preserving our history is
not just about nostalgia; it's crucial for enhancing our community’s economic, cultural, and
aesthetic value.

Criteria for Preservation: An updated ordinance will clearly define processes and criteria for
designating and protecting local historic districts, something missing in our current framework.
The current ordinance does not recognize or apply to the new Yoshiko Yamanouchi House
Historic District or the pending Baywood Historic District.

Legal Clarity and Protection: It will provide a robust legal framework to recognize, protect, and
manage historic resources, ensuring they are considered in development reviews.

www.smheritage.org
131 of 426


--- page 132 ---
City Council
January 16, 2025
Page 2

The Urgency of Action
e Time is of the Essence: Over three decades have passed since significant action was taken on
historic preservation in San Mateo. Delaying further will only increase costs and risks losing
more of our heritage.

e Resource Allocation: With budgets potentially tightening, acting now is prudent to leverage
existing funds for maximum impact.

Balancing Historic Preservation with Housing Needs
e Compatibility with Modern Needs: Historic properties and districts can accommodate modern
housing solutions like ADUs, expansions, and remodels, proving that preservation does not
hinder but can complement urban development.

e Selective Designation: The criteria for historic designation are stringent, ensuring only truly
significant structures or neighborhoods are protected, thus not broadly impeding new housing
developments.

In conclusion, the time to act is now to safeguard San Mateo’s historical narrative while fostering
growth. Approving this scope of work will not only protect our past but also enrich our future. We
urge you to ignore the misinformation and support this initiative for the benefit of San Mateo's cultural
heritage and its residents.

Thank you for your consideration.

Sincerely,

Laurie Hietter
President
San Mateo Heritage Alliance

Ok Outlook

Against Historic District Designations

From Paul Dagnelc <a

Date Wed 1/15/2025 1:02 PM

Dear San Mateo City Council,

As a resident of San Mateo, | ask that you reject the proposal to establish new historic districts in any
neighborhoods. San Mateo is a wonderful, vibrant city, but is suffering from serious housing
affordability issues. Historic districts will make it harder and more expensive to build new homes,
preventing us from making progress on this important issue.

At both the state and local level we have passed good housing laws, but historic districts would
undermine both those laws (including Measure T, which just passed by ballot proposal) and our
general plan. Please do not support any actions to establish more historical districts, and vote now on

the Historic consultant RFP. The priority for San Mateo should be increasing housing, not restricting it.

Thank you for your time,
Paul Dagnelie

Dear City Council,
I'm writing to ask you to oppose the adoption of the Historic Resources RFP in tonight's agenda item #10,

San Mateo’s most historic and beautiful properties already have the appropriate protections. The city’s heritage is
not in danger. A vocal but tiny minority has asked you to act as if it is, but they do not represent the city. As
evidence of their misalignment with the community, note that the extensive proposal for Baywood historic
designation was, in the end, opposed by 90% of Baywood owners. This RFP is at odds with the priorities and
desires of your constituents.

Spending more money on studying this issue is a waste of important city dollars. It’s also dangerous. It opens the
door to abuse of CEQA by that well-financed minority, who can afford to hire private lawyers to bully property
owners and developers who don't bend to their whims. Members of that minority have already demonstrated their
willingness to “go vigilante” on historic preservation, instead of trusting our city planning staff, who are already
working hard to make sure that real historic resources have the appropriate protections. City planning takes
preservation of our real historic resources seriously and does not need the intrusion of wealthy private community
members armed with new legal avenues for control.

There are other ways, which do not raise such legal concerns, to encourage and support the caretaking of our
historic resources. | know others have written in with suggestions, Please choose an alternative approach to
supporting the historic portion of our housing element. Community outreach would be a good start to determine
what to do. If even minor traffic safety improvements warrant lengthy community engagement, something this
consequential certainly does.

Thank you,
- Rick Ballard
San Mateo Resident, district 2

From Mary Burns <i

21/01/2025, 10:42 Historic Preservation 7 SY Outlook

Ge Outlook
Historic Preservation

Date Sun 1/19/2025 9:53 AM
To City Council (San Mateo) <CityCouncil@cityofsanmateo.org>

January 19, 2025

City Council

City of San Mateo
330 W. 20th Avenue
San Mateo, CA 94403

SUBJECT: Support for Context Study and Historic Preservation Ordinance Update
Dear Mayor Newsom and City Council Members,

| am writing to express my strong support for the approval of the proposed scope of work to prepare
a context study and update the City’s historic preservation ordinance. As a resident of San Mateo for
nearly 25 years, | have witnessed firsthand how our community's history is an essential part of what
makes our city unique. The current historic preservation ordinance, dating back to 1993, and the 1989
Historic Building Survey are outdated and insufficient for our rapidly growing city. Updating both is
critical to preserving the city’s rich legacy while accommodating future development.

The Importance of a Context Study

e Cost-Effective and Efficient: A context study provides a cost-effective alternative to surveying
each historic property individually. It offers a comprehensive understanding of our city's historic
assets at a fraction of the cost.

e Framework for Preservation: The study will provide the necessary foundation to establish a
citywide understanding of our historic resources, which will guide future preservation efforts and
development decisions.

¢ Informed Policy: The findings of the context study will directly influence the revision of the
preservation ordinance, ensuring it accurately reflects the current state of our historic resources
and guides effective policy-making.

e Strategic Planning: By identifying the type, quantity, and location of historic resources, the
study will enable informed decisions that balance the need for growth with the importance of
preserving our heritage.

The Necessity of Updating the Historic Preservation Ordinance

¢ Cultural and Economic Benefits: As the current ordinance notes, preserving our history is not
only a matter of nostalgia—it enhances the cultural, economic, and aesthetic value of our
community.

about:blank?windowld=SecondaryReadingPane16 1/2
155 of 426


--- page 156 ---
156 of 426

--- page 157 ---
Kevin & Lisa Cullinane

Subject: Cancellation of $500K Historic RFP for Baywood District

Dear Honorable Council Members,

As residents of Baywood and the City of San Mateo for over 35 years we
are strongly opposed to any funds being spent on studying or creating a
Historic District for the Baywood area. As some of you know we not only
live in San Mateo but have done business in this City for over 35 years,
operating SC Properties, a Real Estate Brokerage and Management
company headquartered in Downtown San Mateo since 1996.

Having renovated and/or developed over $750M of projects over this time
we can tell you that we have seen the City of San Mateo go from one of
the most efficient, development friendly cities in San Mateo County, to one
of the worst.

Adding a restrictive component to the already strained and arduous
process of getting the City Planning and Building departments to process
and provide a building permit will only make matters worse. For anyone to
say otherwise is just untrue. While we won't detail it in this letter we know of
at least 3 recent projects (one being in the Glazenwood Historic District)
that took anywhere from 9 -12 months to just get planning approval (then
in one case another 7 months to get a permit). Most of these projects were
assigned to “Contract Planners”, with minimal knowledge and/or
experience. In most cases they became an obstacle rather than facilitator
to that applicants’ project, which should never be the case.

We can say with 100% certainty that prior to 2014 working with the Planning
& Building staff in San Mateo was a wonderful experience. They made
every effort to help move the project forward by being available for
meetings and responding to questions quickly and expertly. Moreover,
staff saw themselves as advocates for the applicants’ project and made
every effort to help them and their consultants provide what was required
to move the project forward in an expeditious manner.

157 of 426


--- page 158 ---
For the Council to even consider funding an RFP for something that is so
clearly an overreach by a small group of residents defies common sense.
We have confirmed with my immediate neighbors (ii

— that none of them are in favor of the Historic District. From
what we understand that is the case in other areas of Baywood.
We understand the importance of preserving our Historic properties. We
own and/or manage several Historic properties in San Mateo County and
have made every effort to maintain them in a way that honors that
heritage. If there are some historic properties in the Baywood area we are

in favor of identifying those homes and working to preserve those specific
properties. That is a more reasonable and sensible path.

For a Historic District to be put into place for all Baywood is akin to using a
shotgun to kill a fly. Please reconsider your position on this matter and
move to reject the RFP currently being considered. We are sure our
already strained city budget can use the $500K in a more useful manner.

Kevin & Lisa Cullinane

January 20, 2025

Mayor Newsom, Deputy Mayor Loraine and
Hon. Members of the San Mateo City Council
City of San Mateo

San Mateo City Hall

330 West 20th Avenue

San Mateo, CA 94403

Re: Historic Policy Update Effort Professional Services
Agenda Item No. 10.
Hearing Date: January 21, 2025.

Dear Hon. Members of the City Council:

Our office represents Less Red Tape (“LRT”), a coalition of San Mateo
homeowners and residents who object to the establishment of historic districts without homeowner
consent. In prior correspondence LRT objected to the scope of work contained in the Historic
Policy Update Request for Proposals (“RFP”), and urged the City to first prepare an updated
Historic Preservation Ordinance, and thereafter proceed with the hiring of historic preservation
consultants to assist with preparing historic context statements that are consistent with the scope
of the updated ordinance.

The intent of this request was to allow the City Council to first establish the scope
of an ordinance (i.e., whether consent is required, whether single-family districts are included,
etc.), and then prepare historic context statements that match that scope. LRT still believes this is
the right path and can be accomplished without an outside historical consultant.

If council wishes to move forward on the agenda item and cannot de-couple the
ordinance portion, then LRT urges the City Council to proceed with Option 1 — subject to certain
conditions. The recommended conditions are as follows:

(1) Consent Based Ordinance: Any ordinance prepared or proposed in connection with
this RFP shall require property owner consent prior to the City surveying, designating,
or listing a property as a resource on any local register, survey or list.

(2) Single-Family Residential Exclusion: No Historic Context Statements or surveys
shall be performed, proposed or considered as part of this Historic Policy Update for

A Limited Liability Law Partnership Including Corporations / Los Angeles ® San Francisco * Orange County

72935831v1
163 of 426


--- page 164 ---
January 20, 2025
Page 2

any potential district that includes single-family residential homes, unless affirmative
consent is first obtained from the homeowners.

(3) Consent Threshold and Process: For potential single family residential districts,
consent will be determined in a similar manner as the City’s Residential Parking Permit
Program: a survey will be mailed to all households in the area, and at least 50% of
households in the proposed program area must respond to the survey. Of those
responding, at least 67% must support the proposed program.

We believe these conditions are both reasonable and narrowly tailored to allow for
the City to accomplish its goal of updating its historic preservation program, while also balancing
the property rights of City residents. To assist the City Council with proceeding in this manner,
we have attached a revised resolution labeled as Option 4. Option 4 simply directs staff to proceed
with the Historic Policy Update subject to these requested terms.

Thank you in advance for your consideration, and we look forward to presenting
our proposal in greater detail at tomorrow’s hearing.

DANIEL FREEDMAN o

21/01/2025, 10:46 January 21 Meeting - Historic Survey Agenda Item Pog Outlook

Qa Outlook

January 21 Meeting - Historic Survey Agenda Item

From Norma Formanek <
Date Sun 1/19/2025 9:49 PM
To City Council (San Mateo) <CityCouncil@cityofsanmateo.org>

City Council Members:

The notion of spending hundreds of thousands of dollars on a historic property survey is disturbing for
a number of reasons.

The tragedy in Los Angeles and environs is one that could easily visit our city. San Mateo sits at the
base of steep, wildland canyons that are choked with dead and diseased trees, brush and all manner of
fuel. If you have not driven slowly up Crystal Springs Road, Parrott Drive, Polhemus, Tournament,
Hillsdale etc. and looked at the adjoining land, | urge you to do so and consider the fire risk. Some of
this land is in the County and Hillsborough, but if it burns, San Mateo will burn too. Thus far this year
we've had decent rainfall. So did LA in the last couple of years, leading to rapid brush growth in the
hills which, with a dry spell and winds out of the valley and desert, led to the cataclysmic fire. | would
hope there is a major cooperative effort with the City's neighbors - with funding_and not just paper
studies - to mitigate risk. San Mateos older buildings (whether or not they meet the definition of
"historic") are_far more likely to be destroyed by fire than developers. The money that is proposed for
a historic site survey should be used to benefit the entire city, neighboring communities and our
economy as a whole by mitigating fire danger.

Further, the lack of housing in San Mateo that meets any definition of "affordable" is stifling our City's
vibrancy. | have lived in Baywood and Aragon for 40+ years -- | want teachers, City workers, health
care workers, firefighters and police to enjoy what I've enjoyed. The San Mateo Heritage Alliance has
been transparent about their goal of "preserving" Baywood as a neighborhood of single family homes
- j.e., without ADUs. While the number of ADUs that conceivably could be built in Baywood is a
vanishingly small addition to the residential stock that is needed, | see no legitimate purpose in
establishing special enclaves in the City or throwing up another hurdle to housing.

It is, further, without question that a historic district designation will put further burdens on the
availability and cost of homeowners insurance. If insurance becomes unaffordable or unavailable, the
economic consequences and saleability of homes will be dire. | hope the City has taken expert advice
on this issue - it is complex but should be of compelling importance to the Council, much more so that
identifying subjectively "historic" building facades.

Thank you for your thoughtful consideration of these important issues.

Norma Formanek

21/01/2025, 10:55 Historic Preservation is not a Priority I - Outlook

Qa Outlook

Historic Preservation is not a Priority

From Michael Hosticka

Date Mon 1/20/2025 9:25 AM

To Rob Newsom <rnewsom@cityofsanmateo.org>; Adam Loraine <aloraine@cityofsanmateo.org>; Danielle
Cwirko-Godycki <dcwirkagodycki@cityofsanmateo.org>; Nicole Fernandez
<nfernandez@cityofsanmateo.org>; Lisa Diaz Nash <Idiaznash@cityofsanmateo.org>; City Mgr
<citymgr@cityofsanmateo.org>; City Council (San Mateo) <CityCouncil@cityofsanmateo.org>; Clerk
<clerk@cityofsanmateo.org>

Dear City Council Members,

| am writing to strongly oppose the proposed $500,000 expenditure for historic preservation consultants coming to
vote on January 21st.

With a $10.6M deficit and $306M in unfunded infrastructure projects, this spending makes no sense. Our Central
Park Playground is closed, MLK Rec Center is in shambles, and other community facilities are deteriorating.

This project, pushed by a preservationist special interest group, appears designed to block development and
create more red tape. Similar efforts in Baywood were opposed 9-to-1 by residents. It would effectively undermine
Measure T's housing progress and put huge burdens on homeowners and eventually increase rental prices as well.

Please prioritize our critical infrastructure needs over creating new bureaucratic barriers. Our community needs
functional parks and facilities, not more development restrictions.

These historical preservation efforts do not reflect my priorities and | oppose them.

Sincerely,
Michael Hosticka

One of San Mateo’s greatest liabilities is our high cost of living, and making it harder to build more
homes will only make it more expensive. Redwood City and other cities are facing this same challenge
without trying to stymie new development.

New housing laws are seeking to address the housing affordability crisis, and we must work together
as a region to create better and stronger communities, not exclude people or condemn them to

megacommutes. The creation of historic districts would undermine these efforts.

Please do not support any actions to establish more historical districts. Vote no on the proposed
Historic consultant RFP.

Thank you for the opportunity to comment.

Anthony Lazarus

SAN MATEO, CALIFORNIA

June 2024 with Thanks to Chris Eckert

--- page 195 ---
PURPOSE OF THE STUDY

The Glazenwood Historic District is a small neighborhood of single-family homes in
the Hayward Park area of San Mateo , California. The homes were built in the 1920s
and 1930s and are primarily Spanish Colonial Revival architecture.

The District is one of three historic districts in San Mateo. The Downtown Historic
District and Glazenwood were identified in the 1989 Historic Building Survey
commissioned by the City of San Mateo. The Yoshiko Yamanouchi House Historic
District was listed on the National Register of Historic Places in 2023.

The Baywood Historic District was nominated in 2023 to be listed on the National

Register of Historic Places. This nomination raised questions about what it means to
live in a historic district.

This survey was designed to solicit the opinions of residents regarding their years of
living in a historic district in the City of San Mateo to respond to these questions.

Due to its small size the survey has an 18% margin of error at a 95% confidence level.

195 of 426


--- page 196 ---
STUDY DESIGN

This resident survey was designed by Edna Luther & Associates, Inc.,a national
marketing research and consulting firm. (See appendix) This firm has conducted
thousands of studies to measure consumer attitudes that inform major decisions.

The questions were developed to elicit unbiased opinions of residents. The
questionnaire was hand delivered by Mr. Chris Eckert, a Glazenwood resident and
local realtor who specializes in the Glazenwood area of San Mateo. Responses
were mailed or hand delivered to Mr. Eckert. There are 37 homes in
Glazenwood. The questionnaire was completed by |7 residents, or 46% of
residents.

--- page 202 ---
RESPONDENTS WERE ASKED TO READ

“INFORMATION ON GLAZENWOOD HISTORY”

The City of San Mateo currently has two identified historic districts, the Downtown Historic District and the Glazenwood Historic
District.

Historic districts typically come with legal protections that ensure relevant buildings and homes remain visually intact with their
surrounding structures, meaning the homes are much like they were when first built.

The Glazenwood Historic District, a neighborhood of single-family homes within Hayward Park, was designated a local historic
district by the City in the early 1990s and is eligible for the National Register of Historic Places. The District retains a high degree of
integrity.

Glazenwood now occupies the site of the original Hayward mansion which was converted to the luxury Peninsula Hotel after
Hayward’s death. The Hotel burned down in 1920.

Between 1922 and | 925, the S.A. Born Building Company developed the property into an upscale residential area of Spanish
Colonial Revival homes. One distinguishing feature of the subdivision is its U-shaped design with the two curved streets of Laurel
and Rosewood. Curved streets were popular at the time, derived from the country lanes of England.

The District includes a majority of houses on the west side of Rosewood Drive, Laurel Avenue, the 100 block of Hayward Avenue
and the east side of Palm Avenue between 9th and Hayward.

The boundaries are based on the original subdivision map as well as the visual coherence and age of the houses.

Perhaps the most striking visual feature of this neighborhood is the use of the Spanish Colonial Revival style architecture. Many
architectural historians note that this style became the favored style for coastal California in the 1920s. In fact, if one architectural
style were selected to characterize San Mateo’s historic building stock, the most likely choice would be the Spanish Colonial Revival.

One historian described the neighborhood this way, “Glazenwood epitomizes San Mateo’s hopes during the | 920s, as it formed ee
itself into a community of ‘beautiful homes”

202 of 426

SUMMARY

88.2% of residents were aware of the Historic District when asked.
88.3 % of owners are proud to live in a designated Historic District.

41.1% of owners said the Historic District designation favorably impacted their
decision to buy, but 29.5% of people were not aware. (see slide 7)

Glazenwood residents regard historic designation as extremely important to
the character of the neighborhood.

City ordinances are working to support Glazenwood.

Only one party had something bad to say about the ordinance process.

207 of 426

CONCLUSIONS

Glazenwood residents regard Historic Designation as extremely important to
the neighborhood.

City ordinances are viewed as working well in support of Glazenwood.
Only one party had something bad to say about the ordinance process.

There is no reason to assume new city rules would make Historic
Designation less appealing citywide than it is in Glazenwood.

21/01/2025, 13:57 No Consent, No Historic: Vote "Option 3" on Jan 21 - a. Outlook

Ge Outlook
No Consent, No Historic: Vote "Option 3" on Jan 21

Date Tue 1/21/2025 10:20 AM

To Rob Newsom <rnewsom@cityofsanmateo.org>; Adam Loraine <aloraine@cityofsanmateo.org>; Danielle
Cwirko-Godycki <dcwirkagodycki@cityofsanmateo.org>; Nicole Fernandez
<nfernandez@cityofsanmateo.org>; City Mgr <citymgr@cityofsanmateo.org>; City Council (San Mateo)
<CityCouncil@cityofsanmateo.org>; Clerk <clerk@cityofsanmateo.org>

Honorable Councilmembers,

Please reject unchecked, unconsented historic preservation in San Mateo and vote "Option 3" at
today's Council meeting. The proposed RFP is:

1) An expensive boondoggle in a year when San Mateo is already facing a $10.7 million dollar
budget deficit. We're not fooled by this being funded from the “Advance Planning" fund: at the end
of the day this is taxpayer money, plain and simple. Meanwhile, every time | walk through Central Park
| am furious because our city's crown jewel park has a playground that is barely usable by children. The
same slides that my child (now 20 years old) once played on are gone or in ruins.

2) Not what the people want. Documented formal opposition is running 9:1 in Baywood. Your
inboxes are flooded with opposition, and you will see us in force tonight at the meeting as well.

3) Unnecessary. Why do we need to hire consultants to tell San Mateo what to preserve and how to
preserve it? We live here, we should be able to establish our own priorities around preservation. And
we already employ a city staff and attorney more than capable of writing laws.

4) Likely to create new historic districts even if that is not the intent. City Council will be paying to
do the Heritage Alliance's work for them. The San Mateo Heritage Alliance has already shown they
don't care about a local process and have bypassed the local process to go directly to the state. The
SMHA will almost certainly use the context statements created by the RFP to create new state-level
historic districts, bypassing council *again*. You can't say you weren't warned.

We have attempted to engage constructively with City staff to develop a plan that incorporates owner
consent, but staff has ignored us and presented an RFP that does not guarantee any owner consent. If
Council votes down the RFP, Less Red Tape will be happy to sit down and help negotiate for a better
path forward that incorporates consent and other strong protections for property owners and the City.
That is our plan sent by our attorney Daniel Freedman as "Option 4".

We are committed to solving this problem in a way that benefits the wishes of a majority of San
Mateans. The current RFP benefits only the San Mateo Heritage Alliance. As councilmembers, you were
elected to represent the wishes of the people, not minority fringe special interests like the Heritage
Alliance who have no popular base in this city.

Vote "Option 3". No consent, no historic. If you must spend taxpayer money on something only a tiny
fringe minority wants, please go with our "Option 4" that preserves homeowner consent in the
process.

Historic Preservation is not a Priority

From Shihomi K. Yamanokuchi A, = =—t—‘“‘a‘_OSOSC:~S

Date Mon 1/20/2025 9:00 AM

To Rob Newsom <rnewsom@cityofsanmateo.org>; Adam Loraine <aloraine@cityofsanmateo.org>; Danielle
Cwirko-Godycki <dcwirkogodycki@cityofsanmateo.org>; Nicole Fernandez
<nfernandez@cityofsanmateo.org>; Lisa Diaz Nash <Idiaznash@cityofsanmateo.org>; City Mgr
<citymgr@cityofsanmateo.org>; City Council (San Mateo) <CityCouncil@cityofsanmateo.org>; Clerk
<clerk@cityofsanmateo.org>

Dear City Council Members,

| am writing to strongly oppose the proposed $500,000 expenditure for historic preservation consultants coming to
vote on January 21st.

With a $10.6M deficit and $306M in unfunded infrastructure projects, this spending makes no sense. Our Central
Park Playground is closed, MLK Rec Center is in shambles, and other community facilities are deteriorating.

This project, pushed by a preservationist special interest group, appears designed to block development and
create more red tape. Similar efforts in Baywood were opposed 9-to-1 by residents. It would effectively undermine
Measure T's housing progress and put huge burdens on homeowners and eventually increase rental prices as well.

Please prioritize our critical infrastructure needs over creating new bureaucratic barriers. Our community needs
functional parks and facilities, not more development restrictions.

These historical preservation efforts do not reflect my priorities and | oppose them.

Sincerely,
Shihomi Yamanokuchi

-----Original Message-----

From:

Sent: Monday, January 20, 2025 3:45 PM

To: City Council (San Mateo) <CityCouncil@cityofsanmateo.org>

Ce: Clerk <cityclerk@cityofsanmateo.org>

Subject: Support Option 1 - Historic Policy Update Effort Professional Services

Dear Honorable Mayor Newson and Councilmembers,

T have been a resident of San Mateo for 37 years and urge you to please vote YES for Option 1 to commission an
historic resource context study and historic ordinance update project.

Historic Resources have been neglected by San Mateo for over 35 years now, it is time now, YES, NOW, to
understand what resources exist and how and to what extent they should be protected. The City has committed to
doing this as stated in the General Plan 2040 document — “Actively identify and preserve historic resources and
concentrations of historic resources. ..”” (page 115 Strive San Mateo General Plan 2040). Again, now is the time to
follow through on this commitment.

We are excited that the City is interested in a robust public engagement program that will inform the community and
allow for community input. It will provide clarity on how historic properties are defined and designated. The City,
staff and public will have a clear roadmap explaining the permitting process for proposed substantial modifications
to historic resources.

Why even bother with historic resources? It is because our history is what defines us, it contributes to our quality of
life and it tells a story as to our shared culture. It is also a selfless act that provides a gift to subsequent generations.
In short, our history as manifested by our historic resources, is the soul of our community and we need to protect it.
A City that does not honor or recognize its historic past is a City without a soul — one that is all about the present
and one that caters to a greedy, self-serving few.

Once historic resources decay or are destroyed, they are gone — that story and that dimension to our quality of life is
gone forever.

There is opposition to this project. The opponents are deliberately misrepresenting the scope of work and the
outcome of this effort — it does not prevent housing in any way. Denying this study will not make housing more
affordable in San Mateo.

There are numerous benefits to launching this effort:

- This work will actually SAVE the City money and reduce risk in the long run. The resulting Context Study
and updated ordinance will provide the guidelines and eliminate the guesswork of what should be protected and how
it should be protected.

- It will also guide where and how new development can occur by identifying the areas of San Mateo that can
be developed without destroying or degrading historic resources.

- This will guide City staff in decision-making and helps avoid irreversible catastrophic actions that potentially
destroy historic resources and potentially embroil the City in costly legal action.

21/01/2025, 15:03 San Mateo Historic Preservation Ordinance - a. Outlook

lo My Outlook

San Mateo Historic Preservation Ordinance

From Oser, Roger <i

Date Tue 1/21/2025 12:59 PM
To City Council (San Mateo) <CityCouncil@cityofsanmateo.org>; Clerk <cityclerk@cityofsanmateo.org>

Cc _ Laurie Hietter <

Sir/Madame-
| am an owner of a contributor home in San Mateo'’s Baywood neighborhood.

We felt so lucky to have an opportunity to purchase this home in 1996 based on its location in
Baywood, near Downtown, its incredible 1928 architecture with seldom seen anymore arches,
wrought iron in and out, natural wood doors, Spanish tile roof and floors, and colorful tile insets
on the exterior fagade and steps... and a few blocks from where | was born and raised in 1955!

While we remodeled the inside extensively over the years, we have worked hard to modernize it
however preserve the original features of the home due to its unique qualities that are
irreplaceable in our opinion.

Many in the neighborhood have also sought to preserve these historic gems, which keeps
Baywood as a very sought after area in which to live and raise our families. Yet others have
begun to demolish these gems to build new, modern homes, many of which are lovely, however
most of which do not preserve the incredible heritage of our neighborhood.

Please let it be known that | am in full support of a Baywood Historic District to further ensure
this incredible architectural history is recognized and preserved for many generations to come.

To that end I support the Context Study and Historic Preservation Ordinance Update that is
currently being considered by the City of San Mateo.

Thank you for your consideration.

Roger

Roger Oser

21/01/2025, 15:03 San Mateo Park / District 1 does not need historic preservation - alternatives? hi Outlook

lo My Outlook

San Mateo Park / District 1 does not need historic preservation - alternatives?

rom Kola schiver {i

Date Tue 1/21/2025 1:32 PM
To City Council (San Mateo) <CityCouncil@cityofsanmateo.org>; Clerk <clerk@cityofsanmateo.org>
Cc = Alex Khojikian <akhojikian@cityofsanmateo.org>

Good afternoon Council,
I'm writing in regard to item number 10 on tonight's Council agenda.

As a resident of San Mateo Park/District 1, Council Member Diaz-Nash, I'd like to specifically address
you here.

My family does NOT in any form support historical districting, and we oppose any actions by Council
that could have unintended consequences for property owners and residents in this city that will lead
to restrictions, more bureaucracy, and cost.

As very active donors, my wife and I are involved in cultural institutions up and down the Peninsula
and have donated extensively to the San Mateo Park Neighborhood Association (SPNA) to care for
and preserve our trees and islands as public spaces - which the city sadly does not have the adequate
budget for. We value history. What we do not value is government (and special interest groups)
encroaching on our private property rights as a form of development control. The city has extensive
review processes already in place to ensure development and change align with the community feel.

Most homes that carry weight in the city’s history are already listed on local, state, or federal historic
registries and are protected. The same goes for the historic downtown of San Mateo.

My wife and I would not have chosen the San Mateo Park neighborhood to purchase a multi-million
dollar property if we had known about any potential restrictions through historical preservation efforts.
These prospects scare property buyers - we know of at least 3 families that scratched San Mateo off
their list for buying single-family homes after hearing about the activities and approach of the SMHA
and potentially the city.

No one in the city has been properly consulted yet. The cited preservation support through the
General Plan input was ~30 unique individuals (most of them organized in the SMHA) over an almost
7(!) year public comment period. | believe you have already received many more letters and calls in
opposition within the past 96 hours. There is no popular support for this, and Baywood serves as a
cautionary tale here of what happens when something like this is done over people's heads.

Even if you believe this RFP and overreaching direction is the way forward, | want to remind you that
you face an almost $11M deficit this year and over $300M of unfunded critical infrastructure
investments, of which almost everything should have higher priority than this RFP. I'm ashamed to see
the state of some of our parks and playgrounds - that has a significantly bigger impact on the quality
of life and attractiveness of this city for all of us.

21/01/2025, 15:03 Historic Preservation Ordinance Update a: OJ Outlook

lo My Outlook

Historic Preservation Ordinance Update

From Francie Souza <>

Date Tue 1/21/2025 11:59 AM

To City Council (San Mateo) <CityCouncil@cityofsanmateo.org>; Clerk <cityclerk@cityofsanmateo.org>
Cc Laurie Hietter

To the City Council of San Mateo -

As a resident of San Mateo, I'm urging you to vote YES on Option 1 to approve the Rincon Scope of
Work to prepare the historic context study and update the historic preservation ordinance. Our
current ordinance is inadequate whereas the new scope will provide greater clarity to property

owners and city staff, and save time and money for both. The cost of the study is less than 1% of the
2025-2026 budget, delaying it further will only see costs increase. This scope of work will NOT
designate new historic resources or districts and will NOT impose any new burden on property owners
or halt the development of new housing projects. It will create a baseline to provide for consistent and
uniform evaluation of historic resources moving forward and increase awareness and understanding of
the factors that contribute to whether or not a property is eligible to be a historic property.

Historic preservation does not prevent housing but it enriches San Mateo and our quality of life.
Please consider the voices or residents in San Mateo as you vote on this Context Study.

Thank you,
Frances Souza
