21/01/2025, 15:03 Historic Preservation Project -n- Outlook

lo My Outlook
Historic Preservation Project

from Libby Tong

Date Tue 1/21/2025 12:40 PM
To = Clerk <clerk@cityofsanmateo.org>

Dear City Council Members,

As a resident of the Hayward Park neighborhood, I am writing to strongly oppose the proposed
$500,000 expenditure for historic preservation consultants coming to vote today, January 21st.

With a $10.6M deficit and $306M in unfunded infrastructure projects, this spending makes no sense.
Our Central Park Playground is closed, MLK Rec Center is in shambles, and other community facilities
are deteriorating. In my social circle of new parents, Central Park is a popular and safe place to allow
children to play. My friends specifically drive from other towns in the Peninsula to visit our parks. The
draw of the parks also increases revenue for the city when these visitors shop and eat at downtown
restaurants.

This project, pushed by a preservationist special interest group, appears designed to block
development and create more red tape. Similar efforts in Baywood were opposed 9-to-1 by residents.
It would effectively undermine Measure T's housing progress and put huge burdens on homeowners
and eventually increase rental prices as well.

Please prioritize our critical infrastructure needs over creating new bureaucratic barriers. Our
community needs functional parks and facilities, not more development restrictions.

These historical preservation efforts do not reflect my priorities and | oppose them.

Sincerely,
Libby Tang

Me

From:

Sent: Monday, January 20, 2025 3:45 PM

To: City Council (San Mateo)

Cc: Clerk

Subject: Support Option 1 - Historic Policy Update Effort Professional Services

Dear Honorable Mayor Newson and Councilmembers,

| have been a resident of San Mateo for 37 years and urge you to please vote YES for Option 1 to
commission an historic resource context study and historic ordinance update project.

Historic Resources have been neglected by San Mateo for over 35 years now, it is time now, YES,
NOW, to understand what resources exist and how and to what extent they should be protected. The
City has committed to doing this as stated in the General Plan 2040 document — “Actively identify and
preserve historic resources and concentrations of historic resources...” (page 115 Strive San Mateo
General Plan 2040). Again, now is the time to follow through on this commitment.

We are excited that the City is interested in a robust public engagement program that will inform the
community and allow for community input. It will provide clarity on how historic properties are defined
and designated. The City, staff and public will have a clear roadmap explaining the permitting process
for proposed substantial modifications to historic resources.

Why even bother with historic resources? It is because our history is what defines us, it contributes to
our quality of life and it tells a story as to our shared culture. It is also a selfless act that provides a gift
to subsequent generations. In short, our history as manifested by our historic resources, is the soul of
our community and we need to protect it. A City that does not honor or recognize its historic past is a
City without a soul — one that is all about the present and one that caters to a greedy, self-serving
few.

Once historic resources decay or are destroyed, they are gone — that story and that dimension to our
quality of life is gone forever.

There is opposition to this project. The opponents are deliberately misrepresenting the scope of work
and the outcome of this effort — it does not prevent housing in any way. Denying this study will not
make housing more affordable in San Mateo.

There are numerous benefits to launching this effort:
This work will actually SAVE the City money and reduce risk in the long run. The resulting Context
Study and updated ordinance will provide the guidelines and eliminate the guesswork of what should

be protected and how it should be protected.

It will also guide where and how new development can occur by identifying the areas of San Mateo
that can be developed without destroying or degrading historic resources.

This will guide City staff in decision-making and helps avoid irreversible catastrophic actions that
potentially destroy historic resources and potentially embroil the City in costly legal action.

January 21, 2025 
 
TO: 
Honorable Mayor Newsom 
Deputy Mayor Loraine  
Council Members Fernandez, Cwirko-Godycki and Diaz-Nash  
 
RE: 
Item 10:  Historic Policy Update Effort Professional Services – Appropriation 
and Agreement 
 
January 21, 2025 - San Mateo City Council Meeting 
 
Please Vote to APPROVE Item 10 -Option 1 as it appears on tonight’s Agenda. 
 
An annual “Blue Sky” Session is held early each year by City Council.  The purpose is for 
Council members to:  share their priorities for the Council during the coming year; 
review/discuss/update or delete items from the previous year’s list; and to gather 
input from the public on their priorities. Updating the City’s 1989 Historic Building 
Survey has consistently appeared on one, if not more, of Councilmembers’ list.  Yet, no 
forward progress has been made.  Please make a move in the positive direction by 
Approving Item 10 on tonight’s Agenda. 
  
Soon after my appointment to the Planning Commission in 2011, I requested a copy of 
the City of San Mateo Historic Building Survey Final Report, January 1989, from then 
Chief of Planning Ron Munekawa.  This survey and resulting 96 page document was a 
joint effort of the City of San Mateo’s Planning Department and the San Mateo County 
Historical Association. 
 
Common wisdom says that such documents should be updated every five years. San 
Mateo’s 1989 Survey has not been updated in 36 years; the existing San Mateo Historic 
Building Ordinance has not been updated in 32 years. 
 
Please make a move in the correct direction tonight by Approving Item 10 – Option 1. 
 
 
Thank You, 
Dianne Whitaker, Architect 
San Mateo

The Inconvenient Truth about historical preservation is that it takes a great deal of time and
money.

To repair or replace a historic Slate or Spanish tile roof requires that the same materials be
used. That cost is double or triple the cost of conventional.

Replacing single pane - divided light wooden window is equally cumbersome. Find it; buy it
which will take and extraordinary amount of time and money followed by continual
maintenance. Don’t forget the environmental impact of scraping, sanding, priming and
repainting every few years.

The fires in LA highlight the fact that historic homes are tinderboxes. An owner in need of
repair and or replacement will have fewer options that take longer and command higher
prices. Fire Resistant, Environmentally Friendly materials and Sprinklers name a few of what
is required by current codes.

These things don’t apply to me you say. Oh yes they do! ALL OF THIS AND MORE

--- page 272 ---
Los Angeles Historic Resources Survey

GUIDE FOR PROFESSIONALS USING THE HISTORIC CONTEXT

STATEMENT FOR PROPERTY EVALUATIONS
Revised August 2020

GETTING STARTED

Los Angeles’ citywide Historic Context Statement (HCS) is designed for use by SurveyLA field surveyors
and by all agencies, organizations, and professionals completing historic resources surveys in the city of
Los Angeles.

The context statement is organized using the Multiple Property Documentation (MPD) format
developed by the National Park Service for use in nominating properties related by theme to the
National Register of Historic Places. This format provides a consistent framework for evaluating historic
resources. It has been adapted for local use to evaluate the eligibility of properties for city, state, and
federal designation programs and to facilitate environmental review processes. Familiarization with the
structure and content of the HCS is critical to applying it properly. For more information see:
http://www.nps.gov/nr/publications/bulletins/nrbi6b/.

SELECTING THE APPROPRIATE CONTEXT(s) AND THEME(s)

The first step to property evaluation is the identification of the appropriate context/theme combination
using the context statement outline available at https://planning lacity.org/preservation-design/historic-
resources/historic-themes. Note that historic contexts cover both individual resources and historic
districts.

Properties may be significant under more than one context/theme combination and surveyors and other
evaluators should use all that apply. For example, a single-family residence may be a significant example
of a Craftsman Bungalow under the context/theme “Architecture and Engineering: Arts and Crafts
Movement” and may also be the residence of a noted person in the entertainment industry under the
context/theme “Entertainment Industry: Residential Properties Associated with the Entertainment
Industry.” Or a Post WWII car wash may be a significant example of a property type under the
context/theme “Commercial Development and the Automobile: Car and Car Services” and an excellent
example of the Googie style under the context/theme “Architecture and Engineering: “Postwar
Madernism: Mid-Century Modern.”

NARRATIVE HISTORIC CONTEXTS

Theme narratives published to date are organized by context in accordance with the outline referenced
above, and are available at https: i j j
themes. In cases where the narratives are not available contact the Office of Historic Resources for
guidance.

272 of 426


--- page 273 ---
USING THE ELIGIBILITY STANDARDS, CHARACTER-DEFINING FEATURES, AND INTEGITY ASPECTS

Using the Multiple Property Documentation approach, each of the theme narratives is followed by a
discussion of related property types and their associated eligibility standards, including character-
defining/associative features and integrity aspects, which are applied in the evaluation process. (Note:
In cases where narrative context is not available contact the Office of Historic Resources for guidance.)

The eligibility standards, character-defining/associative features, and integrity aspects are guidelines for
field surveyors making property evaluations. They represent the strength of the association of a
resource to a theme and identify physical and associative features a property must have to be a good
example of a type within a theme.

e Properties do NOT need to meet ALL eligibility standards and character-defining/associative
features to be eligibie; these are guidelines based on knowledge of known significant examples
of property types.

* integrity aspects and considerations are guidelines for assessing resource integrity within a
specific context/theme. There are many variables to consider in assessing integrity depending
on WHY a resource is significant.

USING THE PERIOD OF SIGNIFICANCE

Periods of Significance (POS) for contexts and themes were developed early on in the SurveyLA process
to guide field evaluations and were based, at that time, on designated resources and known resources

identified through research and previous survey evaluations. Many of these have been revised/refined

based on actual survey findings and additional research conducted for developing theme narratives.

Surveyors and other evaluators are advised to use professional judgment in applying a POS to properties
as it is possible that resources may be identified over time that fall outside a POS and still meet eligibility
standards. For example, a 1961 example of Late Colonial Revival style architecture may be determined
eligible although it is outside the 1960 end date for this theme.

POS end date of 1980: The end date for SurveyLA is 1980 and, therefore, has been used as the end date
of the POS for many themes. In these cases, the end date is arbitrary and should be extended over time.
For example, the 1980 POS end date for the context/theme “Institutional Development: Social Clubs and
Organizations” should be expanded over time to include organizations and meeting places significant
beyond 1980.

Outlook

Urgent Appeal: SAY NO to the $500K Historic RFP

From Paul Labagh [is
Date Tue 1/21/2025 5:06 PM

To Rob Newsom <rnewsom@cityofsanmateo.org>; Adam Loraine <aloraine@cityofsanmateo.org>; Danielle
Cwirko-Godycki <dewirkogodycki@cityofsanmateo.org>; Nicole Fernandez
<nfernandez@cityofsanmateo.org>; City Mgr <citymgr@cityofsanmateo.org>; City Council (San Mateo)
<CityCouncil@cityofsanmateo.org>; Clerk <clerk@cityofsanmateo.org >

Dear Honorable Mayor Newsom and City Council Members,

| am writing regarding the proposed $500,000 Historic Resources RFP. As a San Mateo resident, | have several
serious concerns:

Financial Impact:

* City faces $10.6M budget deficit and $306M in unfunded infrastructure needs

* $500,000 could be better spent on deteriorating parks and facilities

* Less than 0.03% of San Mateo's 101,327 residents are driving this expensive initiative

Community Opposition & Consensus:

* In Baywood, 9 out of 10 residents weighing in oppose historic districting

* No broad community consensus exists for such a consequential decision

* City has conducted no community outreach to determine if this is a citywide priority

Legal Concerns:

* JMBM Attorneys warn of permanent, irreversible consequences in this RFP format

* Historical context statement with potential for CEQA obligations

* Potential impacts exceed those of general plan or zoning changes

* Council is putting the cart before the horse - community outreach should precede signing this RFP

Alternative Solution:

* Implement staff-driven community engagement process

* Focus on voluntary participation rather than mandatory impositions
* Develop consent-driven historic preservation ordinance

* Prioritize infrastructure benefiting all residents

| urge you to vote NO on this $500,000 RFP and instead support a less expensive, community-driven alternative
that serves all San Mateo residents, not just a vocal minority.

Sincerely,
[Paul Labagh]

Sent from my iPhone

21/01/2025, 15:25 Historic district item on tonight's agenda E- Outlook

oh Outlook
Historic district item on tonight's agenda

From Eldridge, Kary! <i
Date Tue 1/21/2025 3:03 PM

To Rob Newsom <rnewsom@cityofsanmateo.org>; Lisa Diaz Nash <Idiaznash@cityofsanmateo.org>;
nfernandize@cityofsanmateo.org <nfernandize@cityofsanmateo.org>; Adam Loraine
<aloraine@cityofsanmateo.org>; Danielle Cwirko-Godycki <dcwirkogodycki@cityofsanmateo.org>

Cc = City Mgr <citymgr@cityofsanmateo.org>; Clerk <clerk@cityofsanmateo.org>

Dear Members of the San Mateo City Council,

I am writing to express my concern about Item #10 on tonight’s meeting agenda, “Historic
Policy Update Effort Professional Services—Appropriation and Agreement.”

My concern is that the survey under consideration is introductory to encouraging widespread
creation of historic districts. This, in turn, would have the effect of freezing in place wide swaths
of our city and rendering them unable to respond to evolving housing needs. It would hinder
our ability to meet RHNA targets, as well as handcuffing the city as it works to reverse
historical patterns of exclusion and fulfill its obligation to Affirmatively Further Fair Housing.

As I witnessed the effort that was initiated in Baywood, I had special concern about the ability
of a handful of folks to create burdensome requirements that would apply to literally hundreds
of others. At the very least, I would hope the city would prevent this from happening in the
future. I would propose that before a neighborhood could be deemed historic, a majority of
homeowners in the neighborhood would be required to give their consent, thereby making the
process more democratic and consensus-driven.

Thank you for your consideration.

Karyl Eldridge
Vice Chair of One San Mateo

*Wire Fraud is Real*. Before wiring any money, call the intended recipient at a number you
know is valid to confirm the instructions. Additionally, please note that the sender does not have
authority to bind a party to a real estate contract via written or verbal communication.

priorities for San Mateo accordingly, withdrawing this proposal.

---------- Forwarded message ---------
From: Casey Dougan <
>
Date: Tue, Jan 21, 2025 at 11:05 AM
Subject: Urgent Appeal: REJECT the $500K Historic RFP
To: <rnewsom@cityofsanmateo.org>, <aloraine@cityofsanmateo.org>,
<dcwirkogodycki@cityofsanmateo.org>, <nfernandez@cityofsanmateo.org>
Cc: <
>
Dear Honorable Mayor Newsom and City Council Members,
I am writing to request you REJECT the proposed $500,000 Historic Resources RFP. As a
San Mateo resident, I have several serious concerns:
**Financial Impact:**
• City faces $10.6M budget deficit and $306M in unfunded infrastructure needs
• $500,000 could be better spent on deteriorating parks and facilities
• Less than 0.03% of San Mateo's 101,327 residents are driving this expensive initiative
**Community Opposition & Consensus:**
• In Baywood, 9 out of 10 residents weighing in oppose historic districting
• No broad community consensus exists for such a consequential decision
• City has conducted no community outreach to determine if this is a citywide priority
**Legal Concerns:**
• JMBM Attorneys warn of permanent, irreversible consequences in this RFP format
• Historical context statement with potential for CEQA obligations
• Potential impacts exceed those of general plan or zoning changes
• Council is putting the cart before the horse - community outreach should precede signing this
RFP
**Alternative Solution:**
• Implement staff-driven community engagement process
• Focus on voluntary participation rather than mandatory impositions
• Develop consent-driven historic preservation ordinance
• Prioritize infrastructure benefiting all residents
I urge you to vote NO on this $500,000 RFP and instead support a less expensive, community-
driven alternative that serves all San Mateo residents, not just a vocal minority.
Sincerely,
Casey Dougan

From:

To:
Clerk
Subject:
Fwd: I urge you to vote NO on ‘Historic’ Survey RFP
Date:
Tuesday, February 11, 2025 7:47:13 PM
---------- Forwarded message ---------
From: Gene Alston <
>
Date: Mon, Jan 20, 2025 at 8:01 AM
Subject: I urge you to vote NO on ‘Historic’ Survey RFP
To: rnewsom@cityofsanmateo.org <rnewsom@cityofsanmateo.org>,
aloraine@cityofsanmateo.org <aloraine@cityofsanmateo.org>,
dcwirkogodycki@cityofsanmateo.org <dcwirkogodycki@cityofsanmateo.org>,
nfernandez@cityofsanmateo.org <nfernandez@cityofsanmateo.org>
Cc: 
 <
>
Dear Members of the San Mateo City Council,
I am writing to express my opposition to the proposed allocation of $500,000 for developing a
historic context statement for the Baywood neighborhood. While I understand the importance of
preserving our city’s history, I believe this expenditure is neither necessary nor justifiable at this
time, especially given competing priorities and the lack of consensus among residents.
Concerns Regarding the Proposed Allocation
1. Cost vs. Benefit
Spending half a million dollars on a historical context statement seems disproportionate to
the potential benefits. Many cities achieve similar outcomes through more cost-effective
means, such as public-private partnerships or leveraging grant funding from preservation
organizations. Allocating such a large sum from the city's budget could divert resources
from essential services like public safety and infrastructure which currently have a $306
Million funding gap.
2. Community Division
The proposal has already caused significant division within the Baywood neighborhood and
beyond. Many residents are concerned about the implications of a historic designation,
including potential restrictions on property rights, increased maintenance costs, higher
insurance premiums, and lack of homeowner consent in any designation. In fact, as
measured by the objections received by the State Office of Historic Preservation, we know
that Baywood homeowners object to the historic district 9:1 over those that support
it. Moving forward with this expenditure without broader community support risks further
polarizing the neighborhood. 
3. Uncertain Outcomes
It is unclear whether creating a historical context statement will bring tangible benefits to the
city or its residents. Without a clear roadmap for how this document would enhance the
neighborhood or contribute to citywide goals, the expenditure appears premature and
speculative.  As we’ve seen, a few individuals have sought to circumvent any local process
through their filing with the State. Certainly, based on the stated goals of this group, they
seemed to be poised to leverage the historical context statements paid for by the City to
314 of 426

--- page 315 ---
make their own Historical District Designations with the State.

Call to Action

| urge the Council to reconsider this allocation and prioritize more pressing needs that have a
direct and measurable impact on the well-being of San Mateo residents. If there is a genuine
interest in preserving Baywood’s history, | encourage the Council to pursue cost-efficient,
inclusive, and community-supported approaches that respect the diverse perspectives of those
who call this neighborhood home (not an expensive study paid for by a historical consultant who
stands to benefit from a local designation). At a minimum, we must incorporate homeowner
consent in any designation process as a fundamental safeguard for homeowner property rights -
No Consent, No Historic.

Thank you for considering my concerns. Please take this feedback into account as you deliberate
on this matter.

Sincerely,
Gene Alston

Dear San Mateo City Council Members, 
Thank you for all of your hard work looking out for our interests.  I and my family have
lived iin San Mateo since 1989.  My wife and I raised our family here.  We
appreciate how you have effectively managed change and expansion so well.
I am writing to request you REJECT the proposed Historic Resources RFP. 
- Parks and safety should be higher priorities for the City. 
- My understanding is that we have a $10 Million deficit. on our budget right now.  It
seems uunwise to do this RFP.  Baywood was 9 to 1 AGAINST the proposed historic
district. No one wants this except a small group of zealots with too much time on their
hands. 
- This ridiculous non-consent historic survey will create unnecessary bureaucracy and
the City will end up spending even more budget on litigation.   We have lived in San
Mateo Park for 20 years and in Baywood for 8 years before that and Shoreview before
that.  I think the gambit on historic district will create a lot of restriction on building,
upgrading and remodeling.
- This goes against Mayor Newsom's much welcomed focus on fiscal responsibility and
there is a MUCH CHEAPER alternative to historic preservation goals. 
In summary, I urge you to VOTE NO on the Historic RFP and support a less expensive,
community-driven alternative that serves all San Mateo residents, not just a vocal
minority.

Dear San Mateo City Council Members, 
 
I am writing to request you REJECT the proposed Historic Resources RFP. 
 
This is an unwise and wasteful use of our city resources.  City resources should be prioritized

9 to 1 AGAINST the proposed historic district. No one wants this except a small group of

spending even more budget on litigation. The proposed survey goes against Mayor Newsom's
much welcomed focus on fiscal responsibility and there are much less expensive alternatives
to historic preservation goals, including standard processes associated with permitting
remodeling and renovations.

record as supporting this RFP, even though it does not align with the preferences of members
of her own district. 
 
In summary, I urge you to VOTE NO on the Historic RFP and support a less expensive,
community-driven alternative that serves all San Mateo residents, not just a vocal minority.

San Mateo City Council Members,
Spending $500k on a "historic resources survey" seems like a tremendous waste of money.
The San Mateo Heritage Alliance ran an incredibly misleading process to try and sneak
through an application for Baywood to become a historic district, and once residents were
actually engaged and informed, they OVERWHELMING objected. Lisa Nash and her
husband were central to this effort, and now it feels like Mrs Nash is trying a different path to
prioritize her own desires over the wishes of her own constituents. 
There is no demonstrated broad community support for establishing historic designation to
areas of San Mateo. Our taxpayer funds should be applied to the things our citizens need and
want - improved parks, public safety, schools, Fire, Police, and public works. San Mateo has
lots of needs that require government funds. A back-door attempt to subvert the will of a
community who have stated resoundly that they do NOT want historic designation is not one
of them.
Sincerely,
Joe Godfrey
San Mateo resident, Little League board member, PTA board member, and concerned citizen

wo-n------ Forwarded message ---------
From: Joe Volponi
Date: Mon, Jan 20, 2025 at 11:38 AM
Subject: URGENT: SAY NO to wasteful ‘Historic’ Survey RFP

To: <mewsom@cityofsanmateo.org>, <aloraine@cityofsanmateo.org>,

<dewirkogodycki@citvofsanmateo.org>, <nfernandez@cityofsanmateo.org>
Cc: Support User >

Dear San Mateo City Council Members

| AM WRITING TO REQUEST YOU REJECT THE PROPOSED HISTORIC RESOURCES
RFP. | OPPOSE ANY ESTABLISHMENT OF BLANKET HISTORIC DISTRICTS
WITHOUT OWNER CONSENT.

I’m not opposed to historical things, but the world changes rapidly whether we like it or not.
Trying to keep things static in a dynamic environment doesn’t make sense. Changes often
happen in ways we never foresee. For most people, their home is their most valuable
asset and the owners need to have the flexibility to make changes to their property to
accommodate the specific needs of their family. With all the change we've seen in our
lifetime and the impact it has had on the requirements for our homes (i.e., additional rooms
for the home office, larger garage needs, increased demand for technology, etc.), isn't it
reasonable to think that the requirements for our homes will need to change going forward
in ways we can't even imagine today?

On top of that, consider the criteria required for an historic designation that aren't being
met:

1. Baywood is a wonderful neighborhood, but as a whole, it isn’t associated with events
that have made a significant contribution to local or regional history.

2. | don’t know the history of every home in Baywood and some may be associated with
a person that made a significant contribution to local, California or national history, but if
that is the case the owners of those homes have the absolute right to apply for an historical
designation.

3. Homes must embody the distinctive characteristics of a certain period or method of
construction that represents the work of a master or has high artistic values. Baywood is
an eclectic mix of homes built at different times with many substantially remodeled along
the way.

When it is clear that Baywood shouldn't qualify for an Historic District designation on its
merit, one certainly has to question the motivation of those who push for it. Are they just
seeking control? The proponents would have you believe that it imposes no restrictions on
homeowners. That completely defies logic and common sense. If that were the case, why
have it at all?

If Baywood becomes a National Historical District, many hidden consequences come with it
for both current homeowners and future owners. It severely restricts the improvements a
homeowner can make, creates a more bureaucratic approval process and ultimately

329 of 426


--- page 330 ---
lengthens the time required and cost to make home improvements.  Further, it burdens all
future owners with unreasonable limitations.  This adversely impacts resale value.  When a
potential buyer realizes that they can’t modify the home to meet the changing needs of their
family, they will not buy the property.  Most significantly, it grants a small committee the
authority to impose requirements on homeowners without regard to practicality, difficulty, or
the cost that will be borne by the homeowner.
A historic district designation is not something we need.  The majority of Baywood
residents oppose it.  Consequently, it is an issue that is dividing our community without a
lot of upside and potentially significant downside.  Individual homeowners purchase homes
in Baywood for a variety of reasons but virtually all of them are looking to increase their
property values.  They should be the ultimate deciders as to what happens to their
properties.  There isn’t a shred of evidence to suggest that the new construction in
Baywood has done anything other than enhance property values. 
From an insurance standpoint, California is in the midst of a serious homeowner insurance
crisis.  Evidence of this is the exponential growth in applications to the California FAIR Plan
(the insurer of last resort for individuals that can’t get coverage in the voluntary market). 
Many companies have left the state entirely while some of the largest remaining companies
have non-renewed huge numbers of existing policies and stopped writing new business
altogether.  All these actions make homeowners insurance difficult, if not impossible, for
individuals to get.  Even if coverage is available, it has become extraordinarily expensive. 
The recent fires in Los Angeles County are almost certain to make this situation far worse. 
For most people, their home is their most expensive asset and it is a scary proposition
when they struggle to find ways to protect it.   
In a market where availability is already an issue exacerbated by the levels of bureaucracy;
it makes no sense to impose the restrictions that come with Historic Districting.  At a
minimum, it severely restricts the improvements a homeowner can make, creates a more
extensive approval process and ultimately lengthens the time required and cost to rebuild
or remodel.  This is the very thing that insurers are objecting to now.  Historic homes are
often more costly to insure than modern homes because they generally are constructed
with older, rarer, and more expensive materials that aren’t common in modern
homebuilding.  Furthermore, historic homes are typically constructed using labor intensive
methods that require specialized craftsmen and can be slower than modern construction
methods. 
Even if you are able to insure your home today, that may not be the case going forward in a
dynamic market.  Insurance companies often have different underwriting rules for “renewal”
business than they do for “new” business.  Therefore, if a home has been covered by an
insurer for a number of years, the agent may have latitude to treat it differently than a piece
of “new” business with the same characteristics.  In other words, if that same home were
sold, and the new owners approached the very same carrier, they might get a very
different answer.  This is a problem all homeowners could face when they ultimately try to
sell their home and the potential buyer can’t get coverage (at least 13% of real estate
agents in California had a contract canceled in 2024 when a buyer couldn't get insurance). 
Also, since some companies have already said they would not renew a policy if it were in a
historic district, carriers that accept business today could easily change their stance over
time.  There is a limit to the amount of exposure a single company can take on in a given
area.  If other companies pull out, a small number of remaining companies couldn't afford to
be the writer for all that is left.  Once they see their competitors refusing to write this
business, they would almost certainly tighten their stance.
In an already troubled market made worse by unwieldy regulation, if there is even the
possibility that creating a Historic District designation would either limit the availability or
increase the cost of coverage, it just doesn’t make sense. It simply isn’t necessary to
impose a blanket designation on all Baywood homeowners or any other
neighborhood without their permission. 
330 of 426

--- page 331 ---
In summary, I urge you to VOTE NO on the historic RFP and support a less expensive,
community-driven alternative that serves all San Mateo residents, not just a vocal minority. 
The city has far higher priorities, especially with a $10.6M budget shortfall! 
Sincerely
Joe Volponi

Subject: REJECT THE $500K HISTORIC RFP
Dear Honorable Mayor Newsom and City Council Members,
I am writing to request you REJECT the proposed $500,000 Historic Resources RFP. As a long-time San
Mateo resident, I have several serious concerns:
**Financial Impact:**
• City faces $10.6M budget deficit and $306M in unfunded infrastructure needs
• $500,000 could be better spent on deteriorating parks and facilities
• Less than 0.03% of San Mateo's 101,327 residents are driving this expensive initiative
**Community Opposition & Consensus:**
• In Baywood, 9 out of 10 residents weighing in oppose historic districting
• No broad community consensus exists for such a consequential decision
• City has conducted no community outreach to determine if this is a citywide priority
**Legal Concerns:**
• JMBM Attorneys warn of permanent, irreversible consequences in this RFP format
• Historical context statement with potential for CEQA obligations
• Potential impacts exceed those of general plan or zoning changes
• Council is putting the cart before the horse - community outreach should precede signing this RFP
**Alternative Solution:**
• Implement staff-driven community engagement process
• Focus on voluntary participation rather than mandatory impositions
• Develop consent-driven historic preservation ordinance
• Prioritize infrastructure benefiting all residents
I urge you to vote NO on this $500,000 RFP and instead support a less expensive, community-driven
341 of 426

--- page 342 ---
alternative that serves all San Mateo residents, not just a vocal minority.
Sincerely,
Lauren Lum

From: Elisa Radice <
>
Date: Sun, Jan 19, 2025 at 3:33 PM
Subject: Urgent Appeal: REJECT the $500K Historic RFP
To: <rnewsom@cityofsanmateo.org>, <aloraine@cityofsanmateo.org>,
<nfernandez@cityofsanmateo.org>, <dcwirkogodycki@cityofsanmateo.org>
Cc: <
>
Dear Honorable Mayor Newsom and City Council Members,
I am writing to request you REJECT the proposed $500,000 Historic Resources RFP. As a
San Mateo resident, I have several serious concerns:
**Financial Impact:**
• City faces $10.6M budget deficit and $306M in unfunded infrastructure needs
• $500,000 could be better spent on deteriorating parks and facilities
• Less than 0.03% of San Mateo's 101,327 residents are driving this expensive initiative
**Community Opposition & Consensus:**
• In Baywood, 9 out of 10 residents weighing in oppose historic districting
• No broad community consensus exists for such a consequential decision
• City has conducted no community outreach to determine if this is a citywide priority
**Legal Concerns:**
• JMBM Attorneys warn of permanent, irreversible consequences in this RFP format
• Historical context statement with potential for CEQA obligations
• Potential impacts exceed those of general plan or zoning changes
• Council is putting the cart before the horse - community outreach should precede signing this
RFP
**Alternative Solution:**
• Implement staff-driven community engagement process
• Focus on voluntary participation rather than mandatory impositions
• Develop consent-driven historic preservation ordinance
• Prioritize infrastructure benefiting all residents
I urge you to vote NO on this $500,000 RFP and instead support a less expensive, community-
driven alternative that serves all San Mateo residents, not just a vocal minority.
Sincerely,
Elisa Radice

historic district would undermine these laws, as well as our general plan and newly-
minted Measure T. Please do not support any actions to establish more historical
districts.San Mateo has many more pressing concerns.  The money allocated for this project
could be put to better use.

Dear San Mateo City Council Members,
I am writing to urge you to reject the proposed Historic Resources RFP. Approving this
measure would divert attention and resources away from more pressing priorities for our city,
such as parks and safety, while further exacerbating the $10.6 million budget shortfall.
Key concerns include:
1. Fiscal Responsibility: This proposal is at odds with Mayor Newsom’s focus on fiscal
responsibility. There are far more cost-effective ways to achieve historic preservation
goals that better balance the needs of the broader community.
2. Misaligned Priorities: Parks and public safety are far more critical to San Mateo
residents. Allocating funds to this RFP disregards the needs and desires of the
community, as evidenced by the overwhelming 9-to-1 opposition in Baywood to the
proposed historic district.
3. Increased Litigation and Bureaucracy: A non-consensual historic survey will likely
lead to costly legal challenges and create layers of unnecessary bureaucracy, further
straining the city’s resources
4. Community Backlash: Approving this initiative risks alienating your constituents, who
will rightly feel that their priorities have been overlooked in favor of a small but vocal
group advocating for this costly and unnecessary measure.
Finally, I want to highlight my deep disappointment with Councilmember Lisa Diaz Nash for
ignoring the clear opposition of her own district and the broader San Mateo community on this
issue.
In summary, I urge you to vote NO on the Historic Resources RFP and instead pursue a less
expensive, community-driven alternative that reflects the priorities of all San Mateo residents
—not just a small minority.
Thank you for your time and consideration.

Dear Honorable Mayor Newsom and City Council Members,
I am writing to request you REJECT the proposed $500,000 Historic Resources RFP. As a
San Mateo resident, I have several serious concerns:
**Financial Impact:**
• City faces $10.6M budget deficit and $306M in unfunded infrastructure needs
• $500,000 could be better spent on deteriorating parks and facilities
• Less than 0.03% of San Mateo's 101,327 residents are driving this expensive initiative
**Community Opposition & Consensus:**
• In Baywood, 9 out of 10 residents weighing in oppose historic districting
• No broad community consensus exists for such a consequential decision
• City has conducted no community outreach to determine if this is a citywide priority
**Legal Concerns:**
• JMBM Attorneys warn of permanent, irreversible consequences in this RFP format
• Historical context statement with potential for CEQA obligations
• Potential impacts exceed those of general plan or zoning changes
• Council is putting the cart before the horse - community outreach should precede signing this
RFP
**Alternative Solution:**
• Implement staff-driven community engagement process
396 of 426

--- page 397 ---
• Focus on voluntary participation rather than mandatory impositions
• Develop consent-driven historic preservation ordinance
• Prioritize infrastructure benefiting all residents
I urge you to vote NO on this $500,000 RFP and instead support a less expensive, community-
driven alternative that serves all San Mateo residents, not just a vocal minority.
Sincerely,
Anya Wes

Background — General Plan Adoption

¢ General Plan 2040 adopted March 2024
¢ Includes Community Design and Historic Resources Element

¢ Goal CD-5 - Preserve historic and culturally important
resources to maintain San Mateo’s special identity and
continuity with the past.

¢ 7 policies and 6 actions to support this goal

¢ Significant community Interest and comments on historic
policies during adoption process

¢ Focus on how districts designated and definition of contributor
resources

¢ Baywood Historic District Nomination submitted to State Office of
Historic Preservation in October 2023

405 of 426


--- page 406 ---
Background — Historic Policies and Actions

Policy CD 5.1 - Comprehensive Approach to Historic Preservation.

Implement a comprehensive approach to historic preservation based on community input and
best practices from State and federal agencies, to find an appropriate balance between
preservation with other important priorities, such as affordable housing production and
supporting local businesses.

Action CD 5.8 - Historic Preservation Ordinance.

Update the City’s Historic Preservation Ordinance to create a framework for the designation of
historic resources and districts, establish review and permitting procedures for historic
alterations, demolitions or relocations, be consistent with federal and State standards and
guidelines, and align with the other goals and policies outlined in this Element.

Action CD 5.9 - Historic Resources Context Statements.

Prepare a citywide historic context statement to guide future historic resource survey efforts to
identify individually eligible resources and historic districts. If a neighborhood is identified as a
historic district, prepare a more detailed historic context statement for that individual

,, neighborhood. (Scope of work does not address second sentence)

4 of 23

406 of 426


--- page 407 ---
Background — Definitions

¢ Historic Preservation Ordinance — A local statute that provides regulations to
applicable nistoric properties.
¢ San Mateo Municipal Code Chapter 27.66
¢ Ordinance last updated in 1993/1995

° Does not align with current standards and best practices; lacks definitions and
clear processes

¢ Historic Context Statement — A written document to organize information on
the history of an area, commonly organized by theme, place, or time.

¢ Historic Resources Survey — A process for identifying, recording, and
evaluating historic properties within a community, project area

(neighborhood), or region through the physical search for and recording of
historic resources on the ground.

Background — City Council Study Session

¢ City Council Historic Policy Study Session — June 17, 2024

¢ Considered three options
¢ Option 1: Prioritize Implementation of Citywide Historic Policy Update
¢ Option 2: Update Internal Historic Review Processes
¢ Option 3: Maintain Current Prioritization (approx. five years out)

¢ Directed staff to proceed with Option 1
¢ Update Historic Preservation Ordinance and prepare a Citywide Historic Context
Statement (Actions CD 5.8 and CD 5.9) with robust community outreach and engagement
¢ Includes retention of a qualified historic consultant to support effort

¢ Bring back implementation plan for Council consideration

408 of 426


--- page 409 ---
Consultant Selection Process

August 2024 — Request for Proposals (RFP) published through OpenBid

September 2024 — 7 proposals received, reviewed against 5 criteria
Quality/ Responsiveness of Proposal;
Experience with Similar Engagements;
Professional Experience
Approach and Methodology; and
Cost

October 2024 — Interviewed top 2 consultants

Rincon Consulting identified as best proposal to support City effort

¢ Based on overall professional experience, quality of proposal, responses to
interview questions, composition of the consultant team, and total cost

January 2025 — City Council consideration of Consultant Agreement

--- page 410 ---
Options for City Council Consideration

Option 1 - Approve a Resolution to appropriate $328,743 from the Advance
Planning Fund to the Historic Policy Update project; approve an agreement with
Rincon Consultants for community outreach, historic policy and code
amendment technical support; and authorize the City Manager to execute the
agreement in substantially the form presented.

Option 2 - Approve a Resolution to appropriate $394,450 from the Advance
Planning Fund to the Historic Policy Update project; approve an agreement with
Rincon Consultants for community outreach, historic policy and code
amendment technical support; and authorize the City Manager to execute the
agreement in substantially the form presented.

Option 3 - Do not approve an appropriation Resolution or an agreement with
Rincon Consultants and vote not to proceed with the historic policy update effort

at this time.
